{=Script - Textura semi-quadrata=}\n
{=Status - MS punctuation done; tagging notes and textual notes up to date=}\n
{=The scribe has an unusual form of wynn with an open top. Punctuation\n
is confined to punctus at the end of each verse line, occasionally\n
omitted, and punctus mid-line to divide lists. First letters of lines\n
are marked with red, but only those with majuscule form are here\n
preceded with an asterisk to indicate a capital=}\n
{~f1r~}\n

\'_*IOBAL\n
$/P13GM-Gn_-IS\n
$brother/n_BROdER\n
{=Arngart (1968) has a complicated explaination that the previous instance of \n
*IOBAL four line\'s up is for "Jabal" and this one (spelled the same and \n
therefore \'mixed together\') is for "Jubal", his brother. Both Jabal and \n
Jubal were certainly brothers, both sons of Lamech and Adah. But rather \n
than assuming confusion of the names it seems better to take it that Jubal is not \n
actually named here but that this construction simply refers to "Jabal\'s\n

{=Letter subpuncted and then erased=}\n
$ae:ht/nOd{rh}_AGT\n
{=This is awkward as to word order, but works most simply as: "whoever holds\n
his property by him" i.e. "in his possession". Arngart (1968) takes HIS\n
to be "is" but this is difficult with ALT because he has to supply both\n
a personal pronoun and relative: "whoever he is that holds etc".\n
Morris\'s (1874) solution is even more awkward with HIS as "them" and\n
BI-AGT as "behoveth"=}   \n
